### Question 50: In a regular semester, can I take only 2 courses? If so, how will my tuition fees be affected?  
### Answer: 

Yes, you can take only 2 courses in a regular semester. However, taking fewer than 12 credits typically means you will not meet the full-time enrollment status requirement, which is registering for a minimum of 12 credits per term. This full-time enrollment status is important because it affects various aspects such as financial aid eligibility and maintaining certain benefits like health insurance coverage provided by the institution.

Regarding tuition fees, the policy states that no reduction in tuition is granted to students whose course withdrawal results in fewer than 12 academic credits. This means that even if you register for only 2 courses (which totals 6 credits), you will still be charged the full tuition fee for the semester. It's important to consider these financial implications when deciding to take fewer courses.

Additionally, course withdrawals may affect your financial aid eligibility if they result in fewer than the minimum credits for full-time enrollment. Therefore, it's crucial to carefully plan your course load and consider the potential financial and academic consequences of taking fewer courses than the standard full-time load.

In summary, while you can take only 2 courses in a regular semester, doing so will not reduce your tuition fees and may impact your financial aid and other benefits tied to full-time enrollment status. Always consult with your academic advisor or the financial aid office to fully understand the implications of your course load decisions.

### Question 51: Can I pursue 3 majors?  
### Answer: 

No, the text does not mention anything about pursuing three majors. It only discusses pursuing a double major, which requires completing all requirements for each major. The text also mentions that students can have a maximum of two courses (8 credits) double-counted toward both their Exploratory and major requirements, and that this rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed or tagged. It does not provide any information on pursuing three majors simultaneously. Therefore, based on the given information, pursuing three majors is not an option. The references provided do not offer any additional information on this topic.

### Question 52: How can I change my major declaration?  
### Answer: 

To change your major declaration, you typically need to follow a specific process set by your university. Here are general steps you might take:

1. **Meet with an Academic Advisor**: The first step is usually to meet with an academic advisor. They can provide guidance on the process and requirements for changing your major.

2. **Review Major Requirements**: Make sure you understand the requirements for the new major you wish to declare. This includes the necessary courses, prerequisites, and any additional policies or requirements.

3. **Complete Necessary Courses**: If you have not yet completed the core courses required for the new major, you may need to take those before you can officially declare the major.

4. **Petition Process (if applicable)**: Some universities may require you to submit a petition to change your major. This petition is usually reviewed by the department of the new major and the Dean's Office.

5. **Approval**: You will need the approval of both the department of the new major and the Dean's Office. This may involve a meeting or a review of your academic record.

6. **Update Records**: Once your change of major is approved, make sure to update your academic records with the registrar's office.

7. **Seek New Advisor**: If necessary, seek out a new academic advisor within the department of your new major for guidance and course planning.

8. **Stay Informed**: Keep yourself informed about the new major's policies, requirements, and any additional steps you may need to take.

Remember, each university may have its own specific procedures for changing majors, so it's important to consult the official university resources or your academic advisor for detailed instructions.

Regarding the provided contexts:

- **For the Engineering Major**: To change to the Engineering major, you would need to complete the core course Design and Systems Thinking, one Mathematics or Basic Science course, and one Engineering course. Then, you would need to formally declare the major through the appropriate channels, which likely involves meeting with the major coordinator and the Dean's Office for approval.

- **For the Computer Science Major**: To change to the Computer Science major, you would need to complete at least two Computer Science courses (including MATH 202 - Discrete Math), and then follow the university's process for declaring a new major, which may involve meeting with an advisor, submitting a petition (if required), and getting approval from the department and the Dean's Office.

- **For the Social Studies Major**: To change to the Social Studies major, you would need to complete Social Inquiry and at least two courses at the 100 or 200 level, and then formally declare the major through the appropriate university channels.

In all cases, it's crucial to consult with your current advisor and the department of the major you wish to change to for the most accurate and up-to-date information. The provided contexts do not specify any additional steps beyond the general process outlined above, so the general advice provided should be applicable.

Regarding the additional requirements and exceptions mentioned in the Engineering context:

- **Scholar Development**: You must take at least 1 Scholar Development course (4 credits) approved by the Chair of Engineering.
- **Engineering Major Courses**: You must take 9 Engineering major courses (36 credits), with at least 3 courses at the 300-level or Advanced level (12 credits).
- **Mathematics or Basic Science Courses**: You must take 6 courses (24 credits), with at least 3 Mathematics courses (12 credits).
- **Programming Course**: You must take 1 Programming course (4 credits).
- **Capstone Courses**: You must complete Capstone I and Capstone II.

For any exceptions to these requirements, you would need to petition the major coordinator and the Dean's Office for approval.

The provided contexts do not directly address the process of changing a major, but they do provide insight into the requirements for declaring and completing an Engineering major, which can be useful information for someone considering a change to that major.

### Question 53: What is the process of delaying my payment?  
### Answer: 

To delay payment, a student must request a late and/or an extension of tuition fee payment from Student Financial Services. Before placing a student in an absence status, the Student Financial Services team will attempt to determine the circumstances and request a timely response from the student. If the student anticipates being unable to clear the account on time, they should meet with the Student Financial Services team as soon as possible to request assistance and alternative solutions. The student should provide a written request for an extension, and Student Financial Services will respond within fourteen (14) working days unless an extension has been mutually agreed to by both parties. The student must clear the outstanding balance to be reinstated as an "Active" status. If the student does not clear the balance or respond, they may be placed on an Administrative Leave of Absence (Admin LOA) for a maximum of one term, and after that, they may be officially withdrawn from the institution unless they have contacted the Registrar’s Office and confirmed their plan to return or have been granted a leave extension. The extension must be endorsed by the Registrar’s Office and approved by the Dean’s Office.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 15]
Student Financial Services to request a late and/or an extension of tuition fee payment. Before placing a student in this type of absence, the Student Financial Services team will attempt to determine the circumstances and request a timely response from the student. With this absence status, students are unable to register for new course(s) during the registration period, participate in classes or a Work-Study Program in the current term. A student will only be reinstated as “Active” status if the outstanding balance is clear. If the student anticipates being unable to clear the account on time, the student should meet with the Student Financial Services team as soon as possible to request assistance and alternative solutions. After the approved period of absence, a student is put on Administrative Leave of Absence (Admin LOA) for a maximum of one term if the Registrar’s Office receives no response of return confirmation or no registration in the returning term. ### Question 54: Which major has the fewest requirements?  
### Answer: 

The Computer Science major has the fewest requirements. The Computer Science major requires 56 credits, while the Economics major requires 32 credits, the Social Studies major requires 8 credits, the Literature major requires 6 courses, and the Engineering major requires 56 credits.

### Question 55: How many courses can I take in total?  
### Answer: 

The total number of courses a student must take to complete the degree is at least 128 credits. This includes fulfilling the requirements for major courses, minor courses (if applicable), exploratory courses, electives, and experiential learning requirements. The specific breakdown of these requirements can vary depending on the university's policies and the student's chosen academic path (e.g., single major, double major, minor). However, the key point is that the total earned credits must meet or exceed 128 credits to graduate. The university allows for some double-counting of courses, up to 8 credits (two courses) can be used to satisfy both major and minor requirements if the courses are cross-listed or tagged, but this does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim overall. Additionally, students can take electives to further customize their educational experience and meet the minimum credit requirement. The university also specifies that certain foundational courses in psychology, for example, require students to take six (06) 200-level intermediate courses and four (04) 300-level advanced courses to satisfy the major requirements. It's important to note that while the university allows for some flexibility in course selection (e.g., using any combination of 200 and 300-level courses to satisfy the 48 credits in psychology), students are encouraged to follow the recommended course structure where possible. Furthermore, students must take courses for a letter grade, with a maximum of 8 credits (2 courses) toward both exploratory and major requirements, and they have the option to complete a capstone project or additional advanced coursework during their final year. Students pursuing a double major must complete all requirements for each major, and the university provides clear guidelines on how double-counting works for shared courses between majors or majors and minors. In summary, while there are specific requirements for majors, minors, exploratory courses, electives, and experiential learning, the total number of courses a student can take is determined by the accumulation of at least 128 earned credits, with the flexibility to double-count up to 8 credits between certain pairs of requirements and to tailor electives to individual interests and academic goals.

### Answer: 

According to the given context, a student can register for a maximum of 20 credit hours per term, which typically translates to 5 courses per semester. However, it's important to note that the number of courses a student can take is also influenced by other factors such as the student's academic program requirements, any double-counting of courses, and the student's ability to manage the workload effectively. The context does not specify any exceptions or variations to this rule, so under normal circumstances, a student can register for up to 5 courses per semester, assuming each course is worth 4 credits.

### Question 57: How many courses does the university offer?  
### Answer: 

The university offers a variety of courses across different disciplines such as Economics of Education, Cost-Benefit Analysis, Market Design, Engineering (Signal, Systems, and Control, Computer Vision), Computer Science (Introduction to Machine Learning, Algorithm, Statistical Learning, Introduction to AI), Applied Mathematics (Operations Research, Introduction to Quantitative Finance), Pure Mathematics (Abstract Algebra, Real Analysis), and Psychology (Developmental Psychology, Social Psychology, Personality Psychology, Cognitive Psychology, Abnormal Psychology, Psychology of Trauma, The Art and Science of Living Well, Organizational Psychology, Literature and the Mind). Additionally, there are intermediate and advanced courses in Mathematics, including Probability, Differential Equations, Discrete Mathematics, Numerical Analysis, Advanced Statistics, Statistical Learning, Stochastic Calculus, Numerical Methods, and more. The university also provides research seminars and specific requirements for foundation, intermediate, and advanced courses. The exact number of courses is not explicitly stated, but it is clear that the university offers a comprehensive and diverse range of courses across multiple fields of study.

### Question 59: If I'm going for a double major then how many courses can be double count maximum?  
### Answer: 

In the case of double majors, up to 8 credits (two courses) can be double-counted to satisfy both sets of major requirements. This means that for each pair of majors, a student can take two courses that count toward both majors. For example, a student majoring in both A and B can take two courses that fulfill requirements for both majors. This limit is per each pair of majors and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim overall. However, it's important to note that this rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed or tagged between the majors. Additionally, any particular course can only be used to satisfy at most two requirements, preventing triple counting. So, while the maximum number of double-counted courses per pair of majors is two, the total number of double-counted courses across all pairs of majors (or majors and minors) can be higher, as long as each course is only counted twice.  

<details>

### Question 60: Can you give me the grade translation from alphabetic to numerical?  
### Answer: 

The grade translation from alphabetic to numerical is as follows: A = 4.0, B = 3.0, C = 2.0, D = 1.0, F = 0.0. Courses graded with a Pass (P) receive a numerical value of 2.0, while a No Pass (NP) grade does not grant any credit and is not included in the GPA calculation.

### Question 62: Why and how am I getting academic suspension?  
### Answer: 

If you are on Academic Probation and fail to meet all the requirements of your Learning Contract, you may be placed on Academic Suspension. This typically happens after an additional Academic Progress Meeting. Academic Suspension lasts for one term or one academic year, and you may be suspended a maximum of two times. After the second suspension, your enrollment in the program will be canceled, and you will need to apply for re-admission. To be re-admitted, you must submit a letter addressing the reasons for your suspensions and the measures you have taken to address those reasons, and your application will be reviewed by the Dean’s Office in consultation with faculty and staff.

### Question 63: How does the P/NP grade work?  
### Answer: 

The P/NP grade system allows students to take a certain number of courses each academic year on a Pass/No Pass basis. To convert a course to P/NP, students must submit a Petition to Elect Pass/No Pass Grade form to the Registrar’s Office before a specific deadline in the term. Once a course is converted to P/NP, the grade option cannot be changed back. The conditions for P/NP grades are as follows:

1. A grade of 'C-' or higher is counted as a Pass (P). Courses graded with a Pass can be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses.

2. Any grade below a 'C-' is counted as a No Pass (NP). No credit is granted for NP grades, and these courses cannot be used to meet prerequisite requirements.

3. Pass/No Pass grades do not apply to core courses and cannot be used to count toward major/minor requirements.

4. The Registrar’s Office is responsible for converting the final grade to P/NP after receiving the instructor's final grade submission at the end of the term.

5. Students are limited to taking a total of 8 credits (typically 2 courses, 4 credits each) on a P/NP basis per academic year.

6. The P/NP grade is shown on the Official Transcript, and courses with an NP grade cannot be used to fulfill any academic requirements.

The process involves careful consideration and consultation with the course instructor and academic advisor to ensure that the course choice aligns with the student's academic plan. The student must review the Pass/No Pass Guideline and adhere to the deadlines set by the university.

### Question 64: How many courses can I take as P/NP at maximum and how will it contribute to the official transcript GPA?  
### Answer: 

A student can take a total of 8 credits (typically 2 courses, 4 credits each) on a Pass/No Pass basis. Pass/No Pass grades do not apply to core courses and cannot be used to count toward major/minor requirements. A grade of 'C-' or higher will be counted as a Pass, while any grade below a 'C-' will be counted as a No Pass. No credit is granted for a No Pass grade, and the NP grade will be shown on the official transcript. Courses with a NP grade cannot be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. Pass grades can be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. All courses for which a P/NP, I, W, or RP grade is awarded are excluded from the GPA calculation.

### Question 65: I've failed the GWP due to personal reasons so will it count toward the 144 maximum credits I can have?  
### Answer: 

No, withdrawing from a course does not count toward the maximum credit limit. When a student withdraws from a course, they receive a grade of 'W', which does not affect the GPA. However, if a student withdraws from a course beyond the halfway point (end of week 4 for an 8-week course or end of week 8 for a full-term course), they automatically receive an 'F', which will affect the GPA. The 'W' grade simply indicates that the student did not complete the course, but it does not count against the total attempted credits for GPA calculation or the maximum credit limit. Therefore, failing a course and subsequently withdrawing from it will not count toward the 144 maximum credits a student can have.

### Question 66: What and how do I get an Academic Warning?  
### Answer: 

An Academic Warning is usually the first level of intervention for students who are not making satisfactory progress toward their degree and/or who fall below a 2.0 GPA, or for other reasons such as failure of attendance, participation, citizenship, or academic integrity. To get an Academic Warning, you will receive an Academic Warning sent out by the Registrar’s Office. You are then required to attend an Academic Progress Meeting during which a Learning Contract will be created with specific conditions tailored to your individual situation. The Registrar's Office will be informed as a matter of record and follow-up. Three official warnings shall result in Disciplinary Action, constituting Academic Probation or Academic Suspension.

### Question 67: How can I make reservations of rooms for personal usage?  
### Answer: 

To make reservations of rooms for personal usage, you typically need to contact the housing or residence life office at your institution. Here are the steps you might follow:

1. **Contact the Office**: Reach out to the Residential Life office or the housing department of your university. They are responsible for managing room reservations for personal usage.

2. **Request Information**: Ask for the specific procedures and requirements for reserving a room for personal use. This might include availability, costs, and any restrictions.

3. **Submit a Request**: Fill out any necessary forms or submit a request through their online portal. This usually involves specifying the dates and times you wish to reserve the room.

4. **Provide Justification**: If there is a need to justify your request (for example, if it's for a special event), be prepared to provide details.

5. **Pay for Reservations**: There may be a fee for reserving a room for personal use. Make sure to pay any required fees according to the payment methods and deadlines provided.

6. **Confirm Reservation**: Once your request is approved, you will receive a confirmation. Keep this confirmation for your records.

7. **Follow Guidelines**: Adhere to any guidelines provided by the Residential Life office regarding the use of the room, including check-in and check-out times, noise levels, and any other rules.

8. **Return Access**: After your reservation period, return any keys or access cards to the Residential Life office to avoid any charges or issues.

Remember, the specific process may vary depending on the institution's policies and procedures. It's always a good idea to check with your university's Residential Life office for the most accurate and up-to-date information.

### Question 68: Can you provide me with some courses suggestion to take to major in Math?  
### Answer: 

To major in Applied Mathematics, students should start with foundational courses such as Multivariable Calculus and Discrete Mathematics, which are typically offered at the intermediate level (200 level). These courses provide a solid grounding in mathematical concepts and techniques. After completing these foundational courses, students should move on to advanced courses that align with their interests in applied mathematics. Some suggested advanced courses include Advanced Statistics, Statistical Learning, Stochastic Calculus, Numerical Analysis, Optimization, and Partial Differential Equations. These courses are designed to prepare students for careers in various applied fields such as Economics, Engineering, Data Science, and Finance. Additionally, students should consider taking at least two applied courses from other majors, such as Game Theory from Economics, Signal, Systems, and Control from Engineering, or Introduction to Machine Learning from Computer Science. These applied courses emphasize the practical applications of mathematics in real-world problems. It's crucial for students to consult with an academic advisor to tailor their course selection to their career goals and to ensure they meet all the requirements for the Applied Mathematics major. Students should also consider taking a Pure Mathematics course to gain a deeper understanding of the abstract concepts that underpin the discipline. Lastly, participation in research seminars and the option to complete a capstone project can provide valuable research experience and help students develop essential skills for a career in mathematics or its applications.

### Question 69: How to declare a major in Computer Science?  
### Answer: 

To formally declare Computer Science as their major, the student must complete at least two Computer Science courses (MATH 202 - Discrete Math is also counted). The major requirements include CS 101: Introduction to Programming, CS 201: Data Structures & Algorithms, CS 203: Computer Organization, MATH 202: Discrete Math, three intermediate courses, CS 302: Algorithms & Theory of Computing, four advanced courses, and Capstone I and Capstone II or additional intermediate or advanced courses.

### Question 70: I'm currently under a General Work Program for Experiential Learning but the company do not pay me in any form. How can I get the subsidy from Fulbright University?  
### Answer: 

Fulbright University Vietnam's Experiential Learning Program (ELP) offers students the opportunity to gain practical experience as part of their academic curriculum. Students are required to complete at least 4 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the ELP as a graduation requirement. The ELP is designed to integrate academic learning with real-world experiences, and it operates within the standard operating procedures of Fulbright's undergraduate program.

However, the information provided does not specify a subsidy for students working under the ELP. Typically, subsidies or financial support for experiential learning might be in the form of stipends, scholarships, or grants provided by the university or the participating organization. These financial aids are often intended to help cover living expenses, transportation, or other costs associated with the experiential learning activities.

To inquire about any potential subsidies or financial support related to the ELP, students should:

1. Contact the ELP office directly at Fulbright University Vietnam. They may have specific information regarding financial support for students participating in the program.

2. Reach out to their academic advisor or the faculty overseeing the ELP to discuss available resources and potential funding opportunities.

3. Review the official ELP documentation or the university's financial aid section on the One Stop portal (https://onestop.fulbright.edu.vn/), as there might be information about subsidies or financial assistance for ELP participants.

4. If the ELP is partnered with specific organizations, students should also contact those organizations to inquire about any financial support they might offer.

It's important to note that the availability of subsidies and the application process can vary, so students should be proactive in seeking out the necessary information. If no subsidies are available, students might consider other forms of financial aid offered by the university or explore part-time job opportunities that are compatible with their ELP requirements to help cover their expenses.

### Question 71: Can you give me the process of making a Capstone for graduation?  
### Answer: 

The capstone is a culmination to the student’s curriculum to demonstrate the principal learning outcomes and competencies of that curriculum in a meaningful and coherent way. In the Computer Science major, the capstone is an individual project and can take only the form of a written thesis. The capstone should demonstrate original critical and creative thinking, and we encourage primary research. You should think very carefully about an appropriate scope of research and production for your proposed capstone. Keep in mind that projects for which there is no current faculty expertise may not be approved. It is important for you to consult early on with your potential advisor to ensure the match. Applications which do not demonstrate awareness of the scope and the practicalities needed to realize the capstone may not be approved. The grading process involves the committee including all full-time faculty members, with 60% given by the primary advisor and 40% given by all other committee members. The committee will evaluate the capstone using a rubric provided in the evaluation form. For a capstone by dissertation, the student must demonstrate a strong mastery of the subject matter, conduct original research, and present their findings in a clear and coherent manner. The capstone marking for a dissertation involves two stages: Capstone I Advance to Capstone II and Capstone II Submission, which are evaluated based on specific criteria and a marking rubric, respectively. For a capstone by applied project, the process is similar, but the focus is on applying theoretical knowledge to practical problems, with a strong emphasis on implementation and real-world relevance. The evaluation criteria remain consistent, with a focus on originality, critical thinking, and the ability to effectively communicate the project's outcomes.

### Question 72: What are the grades required to get a distinctive graduation?  
### Answer: 

The final grade for the thesis is the average of the 2 graders. The oral defense is graded by a panel of all IS faculty. See Appendix 1and 2 for detail rubrics on both the thesis and presentation. The total grade of the capstone is the sum of the thesis grade and oral defense grade. The primary advisor will communicate this result and any feedback from the graders to the student in writing. If there are any concerns about the grades, students should first meet with their primary advisor to discuss and clarify. If no agreement is made, the student could request one more grader (an IS faculty) to grade their submission, but cannot choose who the grader would be. The major coordinator will decide the 3rd grader after discussion with IS faculty team. The new grade would be the average of the 3 graders. Any further appeal after this would need to follow official UG program’s process for grade appeal.

### Question 73: How can I graduate with Honor or lie within the top GPA?  
### Answer: 

To graduate with honors or lie within the top GPA, a student should focus on the following strategies:

1. **Maintain a High GPA**: The most straightforward way to graduate with honors or have a high GPA is to consistently achieve high grades throughout your academic career. Aim for a GPA of 3.5 or above, which is often the threshold for graduating with honors.

2. **Take Challenging Courses**: Enroll in challenging courses that offer opportunities for higher grades. Courses that are more demanding and require more effort often have a higher ceiling for grades.

3. **Capstone Courses**: Pay special attention to the Capstone courses (Capstone I and Capstone II in this context). These courses are typically designed to be high-impact and may offer significant opportunities to demonstrate your academic abilities. Aim for an Honors Pass in these courses, as they carry significant weight in your overall GPA.

4. **Avoid Repeating Courses**: According to the provided context, repeating courses will overwrite the lower grade with an "RP" notation, which does not contribute to your GPA. Therefore, it's crucial to avoid repeating courses unless absolutely necessary.

5. **Credit Transfer and Exemptions**: Take advantage of any credit transfer and exemptions from other universities. These can help reduce the number of courses you need to take at your current institution, allowing you to focus on higher-level courses that can boost your GPA.

6. **Seek Academic Support**: If you're struggling with a course, seek academic support early. This can include tutoring, study groups, or consulting with your academic advisor. Improving grades in challenging courses can significantly boost your GPA.

7. **Stay Informed**: Keep yourself informed about university policies, especially regarding GPA calculations and course requirements. This includes understanding how repeating courses affects your GPA and knowing the minimum GPA threshold for graduating with honors.

8. **Consult with Advisors**: Regularly consult with your academic advisor and major advisor about your academic plan. They can provide guidance on course selection, help you stay on track to meet GPA requirements, and advise you on any special circumstances that might affect your academic standing.

9. **Incorporate Feedback**: Be open to feedback and incorporate it into your work. This can help improve your performance in future courses and projects.

10. **Defense Preparation**: For Capstone II, prepare thoroughly for the defense. While the defense itself does not contribute to the final score, the advising team may expect you to incorporate feedback into your final submission, which can indirectly affect your grade.

In summary, to graduate with honors or have a high GPA, a student should maintain a high GPA, focus on challenging courses, especially Capstone courses, avoid repeating courses, take advantage of credit transfers, seek academic support, stay informed, consult with advisors, incorporate feedback, and prepare well for defenses.

### Question 74: How many courses can I take with P/NP grade in total?  
### Answer: 

A student can take a total of 8 credits (typically 2 courses, 4 credits each) on a Pass/No Pass basis in one academic year.

The following conditions apply: o Once a student converts a course grade option to Pass/No Pass, the grade option cannot be changed back. o Pass/No Pass grades do not apply to core courses. For example, an exploratory course can also be counted as a major course for the corresponding major. However, the number of double-counted credits is often limited (e.g., see subsections 13.2 and 13.3). Additionally, any particular course can only be used to satisfy at most two requirements. For instance, if course X is cross-listed between major A and major B and tagged by minor C, then X can be used to fulfill the requirements of major A and major B, or major A and minor C, or major B and minor C. Triple counting is not allowed. 13.9  Maximal Length of Study Fulbright follows MOET regulations, which state that the maximum time to complete the program cannot exceed double the standard

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 38]

### Question 76: How many types of leave of absence are there and how can I have one?  
### Answer: 

There are three types of leave of absence: personal leave, medical leave, and administrative leave of absence. To have one, you need to fill out the Leave of Absence form provided by your institution, specifying the duration and reason for your leave. You must also meet with your academic advisor to discuss a plan to complete your degree. For personal and medical leaves, you need to provide detailed reasons and possibly documentation, such as a doctor's note for medical leave. For administrative leave of absence due to an outstanding student account balance, you must contact Student Financial Services to request a late payment or extension. The institution will review your circumstances and may place you on an administrative leave of absence if necessary. It's important to note that indefinite leaves are not permitted, and you must have a clear plan for returning to complete your degree. Additionally, if you are a residential student, you may need to discuss your living arrangements with Residential Life.

### Question 77: How can I report violation of Academic environment anonymously?  
### Answer: 

If you wish to report a violation of academic integrity anonymously, you should contact the appropriate office at your institution. Many universities have a confidential reporting system in place for such situations. Here's how you might proceed:

1. **Check your institution's website**: Look for a section on academic integrity or student conduct. There might be a specific form or process outlined for reporting violations anonymously.

2. **Contact the Office of the Registrar**: They often handle academic matters and might have a confidential process for reporting academic integrity violations.

3. **Reach out to the Dean's Office**: Deans are typically involved in academic matters and may have a confidential way to report concerns.

4. **Use an anonymous reporting system**: Some institutions have an anonymous reporting hotline or an online portal where you can submit concerns without revealing your identity.

5. **Consult with a trusted advisor**: Advisors or counselors might be able to guide you on the best way to report a violation while maintaining your anonymity.

6. **Follow the instructions provided**: If you find a form or process for reporting, carefully follow the instructions provided. This might include filling out a form, providing as much detail as possible without revealing your identity, and submitting it through a secure channel.

7. **Be specific and factual**: When reporting, provide as much detail as possible about the violation, including who was involved, what happened, and when it occurred. However, avoid including any personal information that could identify you.

8. **Keep a record**: It's a good practice to keep a copy of any correspondence or documentation you submit, just in case you need to reference it later.

Remember, the goal is to ensure that the academic integrity of the institution is maintained while also protecting your privacy. Each institution may have its own specific procedures, so it's important to familiarize yourself with the appropriate steps for your particular educational setting.

### Question 78: Where can I get all forms and pdf related to my academic journey at Fulbright?  
### Answer: 

All forms and PDFs related to your academic journey at Fulbright can typically be found on the One Stop portal provided by the university. This portal often includes various administrative forms such as the Exit Checklist, Course Withdrawal Request, Incomplete Grade Request, Application for Credit Transfer, Official Activity Excused Absence Request Form, Undergraduate Leave of Absence (LOA), and the Withdraw from Fulbright form. Additionally, the "Fees and Charges Guide" for refund options can also be found on the One Stop portal.

The Office of the Registrar is usually the central point for managing academic records and paperwork, so any forms related to academic affairs, such as the Exit Checklist with Academic Affairs, would be obtained from or returned to this office. Similarly, Residential Life would handle forms related to housing and living arrangements, such as the Exit Checklist with Residential Life.

For specific forms like the Withdrawal from Fulbright form, you should directly contact the Registrar's Office for the most accurate and up-to-date versions. The Registrar's Office can also provide guidance on the procedures to follow when withdrawing from the university, including the submission of official letters and the handling of financial matters.

It's important to check the university's official website and the One Stop portal regularly for any updates or changes to the forms and procedures. Additionally, the university's academic calendar and student handbook often contain important information about academic policies and procedures, including withdrawal processes.

In summary, for all forms and PDFs related to your academic journey at Fulbright, start by visiting the One Stop portal, and if you need specific forms or have questions, contact the Office of the Registrar directly.

### Question 79: What is the school's policy on academic dishonesty, and how are violations handled?  
### Answer: 

The school's policy on academic dishonesty is outlined in the Code of Academic Integrity, which applies to the capstone. The Registrar's Office informs the Dean’s Office of any suspected cases of academic dishonesty. If the Deans can mediate the issue, no further action is required. However, if mediation is not possible, the Registrar's Office organizes a panel review with the Dean’s Office for an independent evaluation of the grade. The grade determined after this evaluation becomes the final grade. In cases concerning the interpretation of a course policy, the Dean’s Office will defer to the course syllabus whenever possible and otherwise will make a final ruling on the matter. This policy is effective from the date of signing and is reviewed annually for the forthcoming academic year. Any substantive changes to the policy are reviewed by the Dean’s Office and submitted to the Provost for approval. The approved policy is then published and available on the One Stop portal. The handling of violations involves an investigation process, potential mediation, and, if necessary, a panel review for an independent evaluation of the grade. The school aims to be fair and consistent in its approach to academic integrity violations.

### Question 80: What are the policies regarding retaking exams or improving grades?  
### Answer: 

Students are required to repeat core courses in the case of receiving the grade F and/or course(s) counted toward major/minor in the case of receiving a grade below ‘C-’. Students may repeat a course if they have received a grade of ‘D+’, ‘D’, ‘F’, or NP for the course or have withdrawn and received a grade of ‘W’. In special cases, a student may request to repeat a course after having received a grade higher than a ‘D+’ following consultation with the student’s academic/major advisor, the course instructor, and the Registrar’s Office. Considerations will include course availability and capacity in the next academic term or next academic year. A higher grade will be kept and used in the GPA calculation. The lower grade will be overwritten by the notation “RP”, meaning “repeated”, and remain on the transcript. Credits of the repeated course are counted toward the total attempted credits. A student may not retake the same course for the third time unless he/she failed the second time or if a specific grade is needed to meet the major requirements. Students shall consult with their Academic/Major Advisor about their program plan if they are considering taking the class for a third time.

### Question 81: How does the university accommodate students with chronic illnesses or personal emergencies that affect attendance?  
### Answer: 

The university acknowledges that students may experience exceptional circumstances, such as exceptional medical circumstances (including hospitalization, injury, illness, or mental health crisis), close bereavement, being a victim of a serious crime, disabilities where reasonable adjustments are not yet in place, and unforeseeable transport difficulties. In such cases, students are expected to submit appropriate documentation and contact their instructors to initiate arrangements to make up any missed work. Instructors are expected to allow students to make up missed assignments if the absence is reasonable and inform students if they are in danger of failing the course because of class absence or missed assignments. The university encourages students to request permission to be absent at least in advance and to communicate their situation to their instructors. For university-sponsored events, faculty or supervising staff can request an Excused Absence form on behalf of the student, and students must be in good academic standing to be excused from class. The university also recognizes emergency situations where students must be absent from class due to an emergency but are unable to communicate their condition to the instructor(s). In these cases, the emergency is considered a part of exceptional circumstances to be considered.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 17]
EXCEPTIONAL CIRCUMSTANCES: The University acknowledges that sometimes a student will experience circumstances that will impact their ability to fulfill the expectations of the University, including but not limited to assessment, attendance, and paying fees. Circumstances that may fall into this category are: • Exceptional medical circumstances, e.g., hospitalization or incapacitation through injury, illness, or mental health crisis. • Close bereavement, e.g., partner, child, parent, sibling, grandparent, and grandchild. Housemates or very close friends may also be considered as ‘close’, though evidence of the relationship may be required. • Victim of a serious crime • Disabilities for which reasonable adjustments are not yet in place and where the delay is not due to the student • Exceptional and unforeseeable transport difficulties e.g., major transport incidents, cancelled flights. This does not include everyday issues, e.g., traffic congestion, missed buses or trains. • Legal proceedings requiring

### Question 82: Are students allowed to use AI tools like ChatGPT for assignments? If so, under what conditions?  
### Answer: 

Students are allowed to use generative AI tools like ChatGPT for their Capstone projects, but they must adhere to Fulbright University Vietnam’s Code of Academic Integrity. The use of generative AI must be fully documented, including the objective and scope of its usage, the specific tools and platforms employed, the process and methodology of incorporation, and how ethical and copyright issues are addressed. This documentation is crucial for transparency and to highlight the originality and human contributions to the project. The Capstone projects are subject to a double-marking process by the primary and secondary advisors, and failure to adhere to the academic integrity regulations, including the proper use of generative AI, can result in failure of the Capstone I and/or Capstone II. Group projects involving AI also require case-by-case approval and clear assessment criteria set by the advisors. Additionally, students are encouraged to design a dissemination plan for their work, which could include professional settings and broader sharing opportunities.

### Question 83: Where can I get support for mental health treatment?  
### Answer: 

Students can access support for mental health treatment through several avenues provided by Fulbright University Vietnam for their Capstone by Applied Project. These include:

1. **Mental Health First Aid Training Program**: This program offers structured training to individuals to identify, understand, and help someone who may be experiencing a mental health issue.

2. **Community Survey on Mental Health Needs**: By participating in this survey, students can gain insights into the mental health needs of the community they are working with, which can inform the development of appropriate support services.

3. **Public Art Project on Mental Health Themes**: While primarily an art project, it can also serve as a platform to raise awareness about mental health issues and reduce stigma, potentially leading to increased support for those in need.

4. **Resource Guide for Local Mental Health Services**: This guide can be a valuable resource for students and the community, providing information on local mental health services, support groups, and treatment options.

5. **Therapeutic Gardening or Nature Program**: Engaging in therapeutic gardening or nature programs can be a supportive approach to mental health, and students can develop and promote such programs as part of their project.

Additionally, students have access to:

- **Mentorship and Industry Involvement**: Industry mentors can provide guidance and support in developing mental health support programs, bridging academic learning with practical industry experience.
- **Funding and Material Procurement**: Limited funding is available for materials and resources, which can be used to support the implementation of mental health initiatives.
- **Logistical Support**: If the project requires specific logistical arrangements, students can seek support from the Psychology faculty and relevant Fulbright University functionaries.

The **Evaluation Report** required at the end of the project should demonstrate the project’s relevance to psychological principles, its potential or observed impact, and evidence of rigorous evaluation. This report should also provide insights or recommendations for future application or research, ensuring that the project not only meets immediate needs but also contributes to ongoing mental health support and improvement.

It's important to note that while these resources and support mechanisms are available, the actual treatment and support for mental health issues should be provided by qualified professionals. The projects and programs outlined are intended to complement and extend the reach of professional mental health services, rather than replace them.

### Question 85: Where can I find resources to facilitate my graduate program after Fulbright undergraduate?  
### Answer: 

Fulbright is designed to prepare students for work in industry or continue their lifelong learning as well as potential graduate-level studies. To facilitate graduate studies after completing an undergraduate degree from Fulbright, students can utilize several resources:

1. **Program Educational Objectives (PEOs):** The PEOs outline the goals of the program, which include equipping students with the necessary skills and knowledge to gain employment in industry or to study in graduate schools (PEO1). This indicates that the program is structured with an eye towards graduate studies.

2. **Program Learning Outcomes (PLOs):** The PLOs further specify the skills and knowledge students are expected to gain, such as demonstrating an understanding of fundamental computer science concepts (PLO1), which are foundational for graduate studies in related fields.

3. **Academic Advisors:** Students should regularly consult with their academic advisors. Advisors can provide guidance on course selection, help students plan for graduate studies, and connect them with relevant resources.

4. **Career Services:** Fulbright likely has a career services office that can assist students in preparing for graduate school applications, including resume and personal statement reviews, and providing information on graduate programs.

5. **Experiential Learning:** The program offers experiential learning opportunities (e.g., research seminars, experiential learning credit hours) which can be valuable for graduate school applications and for gaining practical experience.

6. **Networking:** Engaging with faculty, alumni, and peers can provide valuable networking opportunities. These connections can offer insights into graduate programs and potential recommendations.

7. **Library and Research Facilities:** The university library and research facilities can be instrumental in supporting graduate-level research and study.

8. **Workshops and Seminars:** The university may offer workshops and seminars on topics such as applying to graduate school, writing personal statements, and preparing for entrance exams.

9. **Online Resources:** Many universities provide online resources, including webinars, tutorials, and guides, to help students prepare for graduate studies.

10. **Graduate School Fairs and Information Sessions:** Participating in graduate school fairs and information sessions can provide students with direct access to representatives from various graduate programs.

Students should take advantage of these resources to ensure they are well-prepared for their next steps, whether that be entering the workforce or pursuing further education at the graduate level. It is important to note that while the provided context is specific to a hypothetical Fulbright program, similar resources would be available at most universities to support students in their transition to graduate studies.

### Question 86: Can you give me information about teaching assistant program right now?  
### Answer: 

The teaching and assessment methods in the Computer Science major are designed on the principle of active and collaborative learning. This approach includes continuous formative assessment of student learning through discussion (instructor-led and student-led), in-class activities, and applied learning. Teaching assistants play a crucial role in this process, often leading discussions, facilitating group activities, and assisting with lab work and applied learning projects. They may also help with grading and providing feedback on assignments and exams.

Teaching assistants are typically graduate students who have a strong background in Computer Science and are selected for their ability to effectively communicate complex concepts and engage students in the learning process. They are trained to support the instructor's objectives and contribute to the overall educational experience of the students.

In terms of the program structure and curriculum, teaching assistants may be involved in the foundational and intermediate courses, helping to guide students through the major requirements and program learning outcomes. They may also be involved in the capstone project, where students apply their knowledge and skills to a real-world problem.

The program description and objectives for the B.S. Computer Science degree emphasize the importance of active and collaborative learning, which is supported by the teaching and assessment methods. Teaching assistants are integral to this approach, ensuring that students receive the support and guidance they need to achieve the program learning outcomes.

In summary, while there is no specific "teaching assistant program" per se, teaching assistants are an essential part of the educational framework in the Computer Science major. They are trained to support the active and collaborative learning environment, contribute to formative assessment, and help students achieve the program learning outcomes.

### Question 88: How can I get the information of campus usage for events so that I can have proper place to study without getting interrupted?  
### Answer: 

To get information on campus usage for events so that you can study without interruption, follow these steps:

1. **Contact the Office of Student Life or Campus Events**: Reach out to the office responsible for scheduling events on campus. They typically maintain a calendar of events and can provide you with information on when and where events are taking place.

2. **Check the University Website**: Most universities have a calendar of events on their website. This is a good resource to check regularly for upcoming events and plan your study schedule accordingly.

3. **Use Campus Maps and Scheduling Tools**: Many universities offer online maps and scheduling tools that show the locations of events and rooms available for study. These tools can help you identify quieter spaces on campus.

4. **Talk to Academic Advisors or Deans**: If you're having trouble finding a suitable study space, speak with your academic advisor or the dean of students. They may be able to offer advice or help you find a quieter area on campus.

5. **Join Student Organizations**: By joining a student organization, you may gain access to reserved study spaces or be informed about less busy areas on campus.

6. **Utilize Library Resources**: Libraries often have quiet study areas and may have specific hours when they are less busy. Check with the library staff for the best times to study.

7. **Ask Instructors**: If you have a particular class schedule conflict, speak with your instructors. They may be able to provide insight into when their classes are least likely to disrupt your study time.

8. **Follow Social Media**: Many universities use social media to announce campus events. Following these channels can help you stay informed and plan your study schedule accordingly.

By following these steps, you should be able to gather the necessary information to find a suitable place to study without interruptions from campus events. Remember to also communicate with your instructors and academic advisors if you're facing persistent issues with finding a quiet study space.

Fulbright is committed to supporting student learning when absences are unavoidable.

### Question 89: I used to take an undergraduate program at another university and I want to transfer credit of studied courses at that university. What should I do?  
### Answer: 

When applying for Credit Transfer, a student is responsible for providing all the information that is requested about the course(s) for which they are applying to transfer. Information may include but not limited to course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments. To apply for Credit Transfer or an Exemption, students should submit an Application for Credit Transfer, along with the required information on the course(s), to the Office of the Registrar. The Registrar will coordinate with the Office of the Dean to determine whether credit or an exemption is justified.

### Question 90: What are the policies of CWP?  
### Answer: 

The policies of CWP include an academic policy that is effective from the date of signing and reviewed annually for the forthcoming academic year. Any substantive changes to the policy are reviewed by the Dean’s Office and submitted to the Provost for approval. The approved policy is published and available in the One Stop portal. Additionally, there is an annex with request forms. The grading scale includes a C+ with a range of 77-79.9%, a C with a range of 70-72.9%, and a C- with a range of 70-72.9%.

### Question 91: I'm a student athlete then how can I bypass all of physical education courses required to graduate?  
### Answer: 

As a student athlete, you may have some flexibility in fulfilling physical education requirements due to your participation in sports. Here are some steps you might consider:

1. **Consult with your Athletic Department:** Start by discussing your situation with your athletic department. They may have specific policies or arrangements for student athletes to meet physical education requirements through their athletic participation.

2. **Speak with your Academic Advisor:** Your academic advisor can provide guidance on how to meet the physical education requirement while balancing your athletic commitments. They may know of alternative courses or ways to satisfy the requirement.

3. **Review University Policies:** Carefully review the university's policy on physical education requirements. Some institutions may allow student athletes to substitute their athletic participation for a portion of the physical education requirement.

4. **Consider Alternative Courses:** If direct substitution is not possible, look for alternative courses that could be taken instead of traditional physical education classes. For example, some universities offer courses in sports management, kinesiology, or health and wellness that could be applicable.

5. **Petition Process:** If none of the above options work, you might need to go through a petition process to request an exemption or modification of the physical education requirement. This usually involves submitting a formal request to the Registrar's Office or the department responsible for physical education, providing evidence of your athletic participation and how it meets the educational objectives of the physical education requirement.

6. **Documentation:** Be prepared to provide documentation of your athletic participation, such as a letter from your coach, a schedule of your athletic practices and competitions, and any other relevant information that supports your request.

7. **Time Management:** Regardless of the approach you take, effective time management is crucial to balance your academic, athletic, and personal commitments.

Remember, each institution has its own policies and procedures, so it's important to understand the specific rules and regulations at your university. It's also beneficial to maintain open communication with your academic advisor, athletic department, and relevant university officials to navigate these requirements effectively.  

<details>

For example, an exploratory course can also be counted as a major course for the corresponding major. However, the number of double-counted credits is often limited (e.g., see subsections 13.2 and 13.3). Additionally, any particular course can only be used to satisfy at most two requirements. For instance, if course X is cross-listed between major A and major B and tagged by minor C, then X can be used to fulfill the requirements of major A and major B, or major A and minor C, or major B and minor C. Triple counting is not allowed. 13.9  Maximal Length of Study Fulbright follows MOET regulations, which state that the maximum time to complete the program cannot exceed double the standard

### Question 92: I'm currently a third year student and moved out of university dormitory after first year but now I'm struggling to find a new accommodation so can I register again for dormitory and will I still have the financial support?  
### Answer: 

The process of returning to the university dormitory and registering for it would likely involve completing an application or request form with the Residential Life office. You would need to contact them directly to inquire about the availability of spaces and the application process. Here are the steps you might take:

1. **Contact Residential Life**: Reach out to the Residential Life office to express your interest in returning to the dormitory and to inquire about the availability of spaces.

2. **Complete Application**: Fill out any necessary application forms provided by Residential Life. This might include a request form, a new residence agreement, and possibly a re-application form.

3. **Check Eligibility**: Ask about any eligibility requirements for returning students, such as academic standing or financial status.

4. **Financial Support**: Inquire about the availability of financial support for returning students. This could include scholarships, grants, or other forms of assistance that are typically available to students living in university housing.

5. **Review Policies**: Make sure you understand the policies regarding room assignments, lease agreements, and any fees that might apply.

6. **Submit Required Documents**: You may need to provide proof of your current enrollment, a reference letter, or other documents to support your application.

7. **Follow Up**: After submitting your application, follow up with Residential Life to ensure that your application has been received and is being processed.

Regarding financial support, the availability of such support would depend on the university's policies and any available funding. Some universities offer financial assistance to students who live in university housing, but this is not guaranteed and is subject to the availability of funds and specific criteria.

Since the question mentions "financial support," it's important to clarify that this support could be in the form of reduced rent, scholarships, grants, or other forms of assistance. However, the university's financial aid office would be the appropriate place to inquire about financial aid in general, not specifically tied to dormitory living.

To get a definitive answer, you should contact the Residential Life office directly and ask about the possibility of returning to the dormitory and whether financial support is available for returning students in your situation.

### Question 93: Can you give me the procedure to request for funds to support club activities?  
### Answer: 

Projects will have access to limited funding for materials and resources. Policies on budgeting and purchasing will be provided. Students should consult with their academic advisor to understand the available funding and the process for requesting funds. They should also review the provided policies on budgeting and purchasing to ensure their requests align with university guidelines. To request funds, students typically need to submit a detailed proposal outlining the purpose, budget, and expected outcomes of their club activities. This proposal should be submitted to the designated office or department responsible for financial support to student clubs and organizations. The proposal will then be reviewed, and if approved, the funds will be allocated accordingly. It is important for students to keep detailed records of how the funds are used, as they may be required to provide a financial report or receipts to the university. Regular communication with the academic advisor and the financial support office can help ensure a smooth process and timely disbursement of funds.

### Question 94: How many ways are there provided by the university can I get the support in my academic path?  
### Answer: 

There are several ways the university provides support in the academic path of students. Firstly, students have access to labs, tools, and software relevant to their project work, which is crucial for practical learning and application of theoretical knowledge. Secondly, support is provided for learning new software or techniques where necessary, ensuring that students are not left behind in acquiring essential skills for their projects. Thirdly, mentorship and industry involvement are available, with industry mentors potentially serving as secondary advisors for Capstone projects or participating in grading as either secondary advisors or members of the capstone panel. This industry involvement helps bridge the gap between academic learning and real-world practice. Lastly, projects have access to limited funding for materials and resources, which can be a significant support for students in executing their projects effectively. In addition, policies on budgeting and purchasing are provided to guide students in managing their project funds responsibly. Therefore, there are at least five ways the university provides support: access to labs and software, support for learning new skills, mentorship and industry involvement, funding for materials, and clear policies on budgeting and purchasing.

### Question 95: Can you give me the information about student fees and charges policy?  
### Answer: 

The student fees and charges policy is not explicitly mentioned in the provided text. However, it can be inferred that students are expected to pay their tuition fees on time to avoid being placed on a Leave of Absence (LOA) status. If a student is unable to pay their fees on time, they should contact Student Financial Services to request a late payment or an extension. Being on an LOA status means that students are unable to register for new courses, participate in classes, or engage in a Work-Study Program during the current term. The policy also mentions that after one term of an Administrative Leave of Absence (Admin LOA), a student will be subject to further action if they do not return or register for the next term.

The policy states that any substantive changes will be reviewed by the Dean’s Office and submitted to the Provost for approval, and the approved policy will be published and available in the One Stop portal. This indicates that there is a formal process for updating the policy, including student fees and charges, as needed.

Regarding additional requirements and exceptions, the policy states that majors and minors may have additional policies and requirements, which should be clearly outlined in the major's description and handbook. Any exceptions to the university-wide policy must be approved by the major coordinator and the Dean’s Office.

In summary, while the specific details of the student fees and charges policy are not explicitly detailed, the provided text outlines the consequences of unpaid fees, the process for requesting extensions or late payments, and the framework for handling exceptions and updates to the policy. Students are advised to regularly check the One Stop portal for the most current policy information.

### Question 97: I'm having some bad experience with a professor teaching a course. The problem was his way of delivering does not meet academic standard and I want to say something about this with people having higher authorities. What should I do?  
### Answer: 

First, discuss the matter with the course instructor(s). If the matter remains unresolved, you may file an appeal as follows: Submit the Review of Final Grade Request form to the Registrar's Office within five (05) business days from the date on which the Registrar's Office posts the final grade for the term. The Registrar's Office informs the Dean’s Office of the case. After investigation, if the Deans can mediate, no further action is required. Otherwise, the Registrar's Office organizes a panel review with the Dean’s Office for an independent evaluation of the grade. The grade determined after this evaluation shall be the final grade. In cases concerning the interpretation of a course policy, the Dean’s Office will defer to the course syllabus whenever possible and otherwise will make a final ruling on the matter. If the issue is not about a grade but about the professor's teaching methods, you should still start by discussing it with the professor. If the problem persists, you can contact the department chair or the Dean's Office to express your concerns. They may be able to mediate or take further action if necessary. If you're experiencing difficulties that are affecting your academic performance, such as initial academic difficulties due to language barriers or unfamiliarity with teaching methods, you should provide a letter from the academic unit specifying the issue, along with supporting documents, to request a review of your course load. This letter should be submitted to the Registrar's Office, and they will review your case. Remember to include details about how these difficulties are affecting your ability to study, details of the treatment you've received, and a recommendation for when you might be able to resume full-time course work. If your concerns are not academic-related but rather about the general conduct or behavior of the professor, you may need to follow the institution's procedures for reporting harassment or inappropriate behavior. This often involves contacting the Dean's Office or the Office of Student Affairs. It's important to document your experiences and keep records of any communications you have regarding the issue.

### Question 98: I'm a third year student and don't know if I should do a capstone project then where should I go to get advice?  
### Answer: 

The allocation of an advisor for the Capstone project is typically handled by the academic department or the program coordinator. You should check with your department's office to see if they have a designated person or process for assigning advisors to Capstone students. If not, you may need to approach a faculty member whose research interests align with your own and ask if they would be willing to serve as your advisor. It's important to choose an advisor who has experience in the area of your Capstone project and can provide guidance throughout the process. You might also consider reaching out to the department's capstone coordinator or the academic advisor for your major to get advice on how to find a suitable advisor. Remember that the advising process is collaborative, so it's important to communicate your interests and goals clearly to your advisor to ensure a productive and successful Capstone experience.

For such students, the Capstone year provides time and guidance that is unparalleled by any course or other opportunity at the undergraduate level. ### Question 99: I'm a member of Fulbright Basketball Club and going to attend a tournament. I need the official transcript and asking for some absence in classes then where should I get help?  
### Answer: 

For requesting an official transcript, you should contact the Office of the Registrar at Fulbright. They can provide you with the necessary documentation and guide you through the process of obtaining an official transcript. As for asking for some absence in classes due to the tournament, you should fill out the "Official Activity Excused Absence Request Form" found in the list of forms provided in the context. This form is designed for students to request excused absences for university-sponsored events and activities, which includes participating in recognized clubs and tournaments. Submit this form to the Office of the Registrar or the Academic Affairs department for approval. They will review your request and inform you whether your absence is approved. Remember to provide as much notice as possible to your instructors, as per the attendance policy, which encourages students to discuss general absences directly with their instructors. It's also important to follow the specific procedures outlined in the exit checklist to ensure a smooth departure from Fulbright if your absence leads to a withdrawal from the program.

### Question 101: How can I borrow books from the library?  
### Answer: 

To borrow books from the library, you typically need to follow these steps:

1. **Library Access**: Ensure you have access to the library. This could be through a student ID, library card, or other forms of identification provided by the institution.

2. **Catalog Search**: Use the library's online catalog to search for the books you need. This will help you locate the books and determine if they are available.

3. **Reserve Books**: If the book is in high demand, it might be on reserve and only available for a limited loan period within the library.

4. **Check Availability**: Check the availability of the book. If it's available, proceed to the next step. If not, you can place a hold or request the book if it's available at another branch or has been recently acquired.

5. **Borrowing Process**: Go to the library and present your library card or ID to the circulation desk. The librarian will check out the book to you, usually for a set loan period (e.g., 2 weeks).

6. **Loan Period and Renewals**: Be aware of the loan period and any associated fines for overdue books. Most libraries allow you to renew books online or in person before the due date, extending the loan period.

7. **Return Policy**: Return the books to the library before the due date. Some libraries have book drops for convenience, while others require you to return books at the circulation desk.

8. **Library Policies**: Familiarize yourself with the library's borrowing policies, including the number of books you can borrow at a time, loan periods, and any restrictions on certain types of materials.

9. **Digital Resources**: If the library offers digital resources, you can also borrow e-books and access digital materials, which often have longer loan periods and can be accessed remotely.

Always check with your specific library for any additional rules or procedures, as they can vary between institutions.

### Question 102: How to work with major report?  
### Answer: 

To work effectively with a major report, follow these structured steps:

1. **Understand the Requirements**: Carefully read and understand all the submission requirements, including the word limit, formatting guidelines, and deliverables. This will help in organizing your work efficiently.

2. **Plan and Outline**: Develop a clear outline for your report. Break down the report into sections such as introduction, methodology, findings, conclusion, and future work. This will help in structuring your content logically.

3. **Write the Executive Summary**: Start with the executive summary, which provides a concise overview of the report. It should include the problem, purpose, what has been done, your program, evaluation findings, and their implications.

4. **Develop the Report Content**:
   - **Problem Statement**: Clearly define the problem your project addresses.
   - **Purpose**: State the objectives and goals of your project.
   - **Progress**: Describe the work done so far, including any preliminary findings or results.
   - **Program Description**: Detail your project, including its design, setup, and functionality.
   - **Evaluation Findings**: Present the data, analysis, and outcomes of your testing or experiments.
   - **Discussion and Conclusion**: Summarize the impact of your work and suggest areas for future research or development.

5. **Formatting and Referencing**: Ensure that your report is well-formatted, with each chapter starting on a new page, correct chapter numbering, and a properly aligned Reference List and in-text citations. Check that all appendices, including production documents, are included as required.

6. **Review and Revise**: Proofread your report for errors, and revise as necessary to improve clarity and coherence. Ensure that your writing is free of jargon and mechanical errors.

7. **Submission Preparation**: Convert your report into a single PDF document, ready for submission, ensuring all necessary revisions have been made.

8. **Presentation**: Prepare a presentation to articulate and justify the project’s objectives, methods, and findings through visual and oral communication. This should be clear, concise, and engaging.

9. **Evaluation and Feedback**: Be prepared to discuss your report and findings during the Q&A session with the judging panel and audience. Use this opportunity to clarify any points and to demonstrate your understanding of the project.

10. **Continuous Learning**: Reflect on the entire process to identify what you have learned and how you can apply these lessons to future projects.

By following these steps, you can effectively manage the workload, ensure clarity and coherence in your report, and present your work in a professional and compelling manner.
